Distinguishing Khabar and Insha'
Defines khabar and insha' by their temporal relation to meaning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given Arabic utterance as khabar or insha' by applying the criterion of whether its meaning is realized externally or by the utterance itself.

Core Idea
Khabar reports external fact; insha' performs an act through speech.

Before diving into the two methods of classifying speech, we must first grasp the fundamental distinction between khabar (informative) and insha' (performative). This distinction is the basis for all further divisions. The passage provides the key criterion: whether the meaning is realized externally without the utterance, or only through the utterance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining criterion
Look for the condition 'its meaning is realized in the external without it' for khabar, and 'its meaning is not realized except by it' for non-khabar.
This is the foundational logical distinction.
2
Apply the criterion to examples
Take 'Zaid is standing' – the fact of Zaid standing exists whether the sentence is uttered or not; thus it is khabar. Take 'I sold' – the act of selling is performed only by uttering the sentence; thus it is insha'.
The utterance itself brings the meaning into effect.
3
Distinguish insha' from talab
Note the subcategories: performative (insha') and request (talab). In the passage, the author explains that request has its meaning delayed, while performative is simultaneous.
This nuance will be explored further in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ لَهُمْ فِي تَقْسِيمِ الكَلَامِ إِلَى خَبَرٍ وَغَيْرِهِ طَرِيقَتَيْنِ :
إِحْدَاهُمَا : أَنَّ القِسْمَةَ ثُلاثِيَّةٌ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى : خَبَرٍ، وَطَلَبٍ، وَإِنْشَاء. وَوَجْهُ ذَلِكَ : أَنَّ الكَلَامَ إِمَّا أَنْ يَتَحَقَّقَ مَدْلُولُهُ فِي الخَارج بِدُوْنِهِ وَهُوَ الخَبَرُ كَـ : «زَيْدٍ قَائِم»، وَإِمَّا أَنْ لَا يَتَحَقَّقَ مَدْلُولُهُ إِلَّا بِهِ، وَهَذَا إِمَّا أَنْ يُفَارِقَ مَعْنَاهُ زَمَنَ التَّكَلُم بِهِ وَهُوَ الإِنْشَاءُ كَـ: «بِعْتُ ، وَ أَنْكَحْتُ ، وَإِمَّا أَنْ يَتَأَخَّرَ عَنْهُ وَهُوَ الطَّلَبُ كَـ: «قُمْ، وَ اضْرِبْ.
الطَّرِيقَةُ الثَّانِيَةُ : أَنَّ القِسْمَةَ ثُنَائِيَّةٌ ، وَأَنَّهُ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى : خَبَرٍ، وَإِنْشَاء فَقَط ؛ ثُمَّ الإِنْشَاءُ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى : طَلَبٍ، وَتَنْبِيه .
فَاخْتِلَافُ الطَّرِيقَتَيْنِ فِي الطَّلَبِ هَلْ هُوَ دَاخِل فِي الإِنْشَاءِ، أَوْ قِسْمٌ بِرَأْسِهِ ؟
وَوَجْهُ الخِلَافِ : أَنَّ الطَّلَبَ لَهُ زَمَنَانِ : زَمَنْ حَالِيٌّ وَهُوَ زَمَنُ الطَّلَبِ، وَاسْتِقْبَالِيٌّ وَهُوَ زَمَنُ الحَدَثِ .
فَمَنْ نَظَرَ إِلَى الأَوَّلِ أَدْرَجَهُ فِي الإِنْشَاءِ، وَمَنْ نَظَرَ إِلَى الثَّانِي جَعَلَهُ قِسْماً بِرَأْسِهِ. وَالطَّرِيقَةُ الأُوْلَى هِيَ الَّتي فِي النَّظْم، ثُمَّ الطَّلَبُ يَشْمَلُ طَلَبَ الفِعْلِ وَهُوَ الأَمْرُ، وَطَلَبَ الكَفِّ وَهُوَ النَّهْيُ، وَطَلَبَ العِلْمِ بِالمَاهِيَّةِ وَهُوَ الاسْتِفْهَامُ، وَإِلاَّ سُمِّيَ «تَنْبِيهاً» كَـ: التَّمَنِّي، وَالتَّرَجِّي، وَالنِّدَاءِ، وَالعَرْضِ، وَالتَّخْصِيصِ، وَالدُّعَاءِ؛ لِأَنَّ دَلاَلَتَهَا عَلَى الطَّلَبِ لاَ بِالقَصْدِ الأَوَّلِ.
And know that they have two methods in dividing speech into informative and other. One of them: that the division is triple, dividing into: informative, request, and performative. The reason for that: speech either its meaning is realized in the external without it, and that is the informative like 'Zaid is standing', or its meaning is not realized except by it, and this either its meaning is separate from the time of speaking, which is performative like 'I sold' and 'I married', or it is delayed after it, which is request like 'Stand up' and 'Hit'. The second method: that the division is binary, and that it divides into informative and performative only; then the performative divides into request and notification. So the difference between the two methods is concerning request: is it included in performative or is it an independent division? And the reason for the difference: that request has two times: present time which is the time of request, and future time which is the time of the event. So whoever looks at the first includes it in performative, and whoever looks at the second makes it an independent division. The first method is the one in the versification. Then request includes request for action which is command, request for cessation which is prohibition, and request for knowledge of essence which is interrogation. Otherwise it is called 'notification' like wishing, hoping, calling, presenting, specifying, and supplication, because their indication of request is not by primary intent.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion explaining the classification of speech (kalam). The commentator presents two ways to divide speech. The first method is a triple division: informative (khabar), request (talab), and performative (insha'). The informative is when the meaning is realized externally independent of the utterance, e.g., 'Zaid is standing'. The performative is when the meaning is not realized except by the utterance and is simultaneous with it, e.g., 'I sell' or 'I marry'. The request is when the meaning is delayed, e.g., 'Stand up'. The second method is a binary division: informative and performative, then performative is subdivided into request (talab) and notification (tanbih). The key difference is whether request is considered a separate division or a subcategory of performative. The basis for this difference is that request has two temporal aspects: the time of utterance (present) and the time of the action (future). If one focuses on the utterance time, request is performative; if on the action time, it is separate. The passage then clarifies that the first method is the one used in the versified text (al-Sullam). Finally, it defines the types of request: command (amr), prohibition (nahy), and interrogation (istifham). Other expressions like wishing, hoping, etc., are called 'notification' because they do not primarily intend a request.

Key Terms
خبر
إنشاء
طلب
تنبيه

D) Water is wet (الماء مبلول)

Key Takeaway
The essential difference between khabar and insha' lies in whether the meaning exists independently of the utterance or is brought about by it.

Two Methods of Classifying Speech: Tripartite vs Bipartite
Analyzes two classification methods and the basis for their difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between the tripartite and bipartite classifications of speech and the logical reason for the disagreement regarding the status of talab (request).

Core Idea
Talab is the hinge: either an independent division or a subcategory of insha', depending on which temporal aspect you emphasize.

Now that we understand the core distinction between khabar and insha', we turn to the two methods of dividing speech. Some scholars divide speech into three categories: khabar, talab, and insha'. Others divide it into two: khabar and insha', with talab as a subcategory. The passage explains the reasoning behind each method and the temporal perspective that grounds the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Outline the two methods
The first method is tripartite: khabar, talab, insha'. The second is bipartite: khabar and insha', with talab under insha'. Notice the key difference is the treatment of talab.
2
Identify the point of disagreement
The passage states: 'the difference between the two methods is concerning request: is it included in performative or is it an independent division?'
3
Understand the temporal reasoning
Request has two times: the time of the utterance (present) and the time of the requested action (future). Those who focus on the utterance time see it as performative (simultaneous). Those who focus on the action time see it as separate (delayed).
This is the logical basis for the two methods.
4
Apply the reasoning to a concrete example
Consider the command 'Stand up!' (قُمْ). Its time of utterance is now, but the action is expected later. If you prioritize the utterance, it's insha'; if the action, it's talab. This clarifies why both methods coexist.
The passage also notes that the first method is the one in the versified text (al-Sullam).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ لَهُمْ فِي تَقْسِيمِ الكَلَامِ إِلَى خَبَرٍ وَغَيْرِهِ طَرِيقَتَيْنِ :
إِحْدَاهُمَا : أَنَّ القِسْمَةَ ثُلاثِيَّةٌ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى : خَبَرٍ، وَطَلَبٍ، وَإِنْشَاء. وَوَجْهُ ذَلِكَ : أَنَّ الكَلَامَ إِمَّا أَنْ يَتَحَقَّقَ مَدْلُولُهُ فِي الخَارج بِدُوْنِهِ وَهُوَ الخَبَرُ كَـ : «زَيْدٍ قَائِم»، وَإِمَّا أَنْ لَا يَتَحَقَّقَ مَدْلُولُهُ إِلَّا بِهِ، وَهَذَا إِمَّا أَنْ يُفَارِقَ مَعْنَاهُ زَمَنَ التَّكَلُم بِهِ وَهُوَ الإِنْشَاءُ كَـ: «بِعْتُ ، وَ أَنْكَحْتُ ، وَإِمَّا أَنْ يَتَأَخَّرَ عَنْهُ وَهُوَ الطَّلَبُ كَـ: «قُمْ، وَ اضْرِبْ.
الطَّرِيقَةُ الثَّانِيَةُ : أَنَّ القِسْمَةَ ثُنَائِيَّةٌ ، وَأَنَّهُ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى : خَبَرٍ، وَإِنْشَاء فَقَط ؛ ثُمَّ الإِنْشَاءُ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى : طَلَبٍ، وَتَنْبِيه .
فَاخْتِلَافُ الطَّرِيقَتَيْنِ فِي الطَّلَبِ هَلْ هُوَ دَاخِل فِي الإِنْشَاءِ، أَوْ قِسْمٌ بِرَأْسِهِ ؟

فَمَنْ نَظَرَ إِلَى الأَوَّلِ أَدْرَجَهُ فِي الإِنْشَاءِ، وَمَنْ نَظَرَ إِلَى الثَّانِي جَعَلَهُ قِسْماً بِرَأْسِهِ. وَالطَّرِيقَةُ الأُوْلَى هِيَ الَّتي فِي النَّظْم، ثُمَّ الطَّلَبُ يَشْمَلُ طَلَبَ الفِعْلِ وَهُوَ الأَمْرُ، وَطَلَبَ الكَفِّ وَهُوَ النَّهْيُ، وَطَلَبَ العِلْمِ بِالمَاهِيَّةِ وَهُوَ الاسْتِفْهَامُ، وَإِلاَّ سُمِّيَ «تَنْبِيهاً» كَـ: التَّمَنِّي، وَالتَّرَجِّي، وَالنِّدَاءِ، وَالعَرْضِ، وَالتَّخْصِيصِ، وَالدُّعَاءِ؛ لِأَنَّ دَلاَلَتَهَا عَلَى الطَّلَبِ لاَ بِالقَصْدِ الأَوَّلِ.
And know that they have two methods in dividing speech into informative and other. One of them: that the division is triple, dividing into: informative, request, and performative. The reason for that: speech either its meaning is realized in the external without it, and that is the informative like 'Zaid is standing', or its meaning is not realized except by it, and this either its meaning is separate from the time of speaking, which is performative like 'I sold' and 'I married', or it is delayed after it, which is request like 'Stand up' and 'Hit'. The second method: that the division is binary, and that it divides into informative and performative only; then the performative divides into request and notification. So the difference between the two methods is concerning request: is it included in performative or is it an independent division? And the reason for the difference: that request has two times: present time which is the time of request, and future time which is the time of the event. So whoever looks at the first includes it in performative, and whoever looks at the second makes it an independent division. The first method is the one in the versification. Then request includes request for action which is command, request for cessation which is prohibition, and request for knowledge of essence which is interrogation. Otherwise it is called 'notification' like wishing, hoping, calling, presenting, specifying, and supplication, because their indication of request is not by primary intent.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion explaining the classification of speech (kalam). The commentator presents two ways to divide speech. The first method is a triple division: informative (khabar), request (talab), and performative (insha'). The informative is when the meaning is realized externally independent of the utterance, e.g., 'Zaid is standing'. The performative is when the meaning is not realized except by the utterance and is simultaneous with it, e.g., 'I sell' or 'I marry'. The request is when the meaning is delayed, e.g., 'Stand up'. The second method is a binary division: informative and performative, then performative is subdivided into request (talab) and notification (tanbih). The key difference is whether request is considered a separate division or a subcategory of performative. The basis for this difference is that request has two temporal aspects: the time of utterance (present) and the time of the action (future). If one focuses on the utterance time, request is performative; if on the action time, it is separate. The passage then clarifies that the first method is the one used in the versified text (al-Sullam). Finally, it defines the types of request: command (amr), prohibition (nahy), and interrogation (istifham). Other expressions like wishing, hoping, etc., are called 'notification' because they do not primarily intend a request.

Key Terms
خبر
إنشاء
طلب
تنبيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the disagreement over whether talab is part of insha' or independent?
A) The semantic content of talab
B) The temporal aspects of talab (present vs future)
C) The grammatical form of talab sentences
D) The presence of a performative verb in talab

Key Takeaway
The two methods of classifying speech—tripartite and bipartite—offer different logical perspectives on the same linguistic reality, rooted in the temporal nature of request.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the bipartite method, classify the following utterances: 'Be merciful' (ارحم), 'I hope you come' (أرجو أن تأتي), 'Is Zaid present?' (هل زید حاضر). For each, explain whether it falls under talab or tanbih.
?
Write a short paragraph arguing whether the command 'Allah commands you to be just' (إن الله يأمر بالعدل) should be considered insha' or talab according to each method. Which method gives a clearer logical picture?

Propositions

Definition of a Proposition: The 'By Itself' Condition
Author defines proposition with the phrase 'by itself'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition 'by itself' (lidhatihi) to determine if an utterance qualifies as a proposition.

Core Idea
A proposition is an utterance that bears truth and falsehood intrinsically.

In this passage, the commentator explains why the definition of a proposition includes the phrase 'by itself'. This condition excludes expressions that only imply a truth-apt statement. Mastering this distinction is essential for precise logical analysis.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Locate the definition in the Arabic: 'احْتَمَلَ الصِّدْقَ وَالْكَذِبَ لِذَاتِهِ'. Notice the phrase 'لِذَاتِهِ' (by itself).
2
Understand the role of 'by itself'
The phrase restricts truth-aptitude to intrinsic property. An utterance is a proposition only if it is truth-apt in its own right, not through external implication.
3
Contrast with external implication
Performatives like commands and questions are not truth-apt in themselves. For example, 'Give me water' as a request is neither true nor false, though it implies a declarative statement ('he is thirsty').
4
Test examples
Apply the condition: Is 'The world is created' a proposition? Yes, it is truth-apt by itself. Is 'O God, forgive me' a proposition? No, it is a performative prayer, not truth-apt intrinsically.
Refer to the passage's discussion of اسقني ماء.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في القضايا وأحكامها

وَقَوْلُهُ : احْتَمَلَ الصِّدْقَ . .. إلخ » :

- مُخْرِجٌ لِلمُرَكَبِ النَّاقِصِ تَقْيِيدِيَّا كَـ : الحَيَوَانِ النَّاطِقِ .

أَوْ إِضَافِيًّا كَـ: «غُلَامِ زَيْدِ».

- وَمُخْرِجٌ أَيْضاً : لِلإِنْشَاءَاتِ، فَإِنَّ هَذِهِ الأُمُورَ لَا تَحْتَمِلُ الصِّدْقَ وَالكَذَبِ لِذَاتِهَا . وَقَدْ تَحْتَمِلُهُ لِأَمْرٍ خَارِجِ عَنْهَا ، نَحْوُ : اسْقِنِي مَاءً» ، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ مِنْ حَيْثُ مَنْهُومُ الطَّلَبِ صِدْقاً وَلَا كَذِباً ، لَكِنَّهُ يَسْتَلْزِمُ بِحَسَبِ العُرْفِ نِسْبَةٌ خَبَرِيَّةٌ مُحْتَمِلَةٌ لِلصِّدْقِ وَالكَذِبِ، وَهِيَ : «أَنَّهُ عَطْشَانُ».

- وَكَذَا : النِّسْبَةُ التَّقْبِيدِيَّةُ ، نَحْوُ : زَيْدُ العَالِمُ، فَإِنَّهَا مِنْ حَيْثُ هِيَ لَا يَتَطَرَّقُ إِلَيْهَا الصِّدْقُ وَالكَذِبُ، لَكِنَّهَا فِيهَا إِشَارَةُ إِلَى نِسْبَةٍ خَبَرِيَّةٍ تَقْبَلُهُمَا ؛ لِأَنَّ المُتَبَادَرُ أَنَّهُ لَا يُوصَفُ الشَّيْءُ إِلَّا بِمَا هُوَ ثَابِتٌ لَهُ.

- وَكَذَا يُقَالُ فِي : الإِضَافِيَّةِ، إِذْ لَا يُضَافُ الشَّيْءُ إِلَّا لِمَا هُوَ كَائِنُ لَهُ، فَبِهَذَا الِاعْتِبَارِ

تَحْتَمِلُ النِّسْبَةُ الإِنْشَانِيَّةُ وَالنَّاقِصَةُ الصِّدْقَ وَالكَذِبَ ، وَذَلِكَ خَارِجٌ عَنْ مَفْهُومَيْهِمَا ، وَلِذَلِكَ زَادَ فِي التَّعْرِيفِ قَوْلَهُ: «لِذَاتِهِ».
Chapter on propositions and their rulings. And his saying: 'it bears truth... etc.' is an exclusion of the incomplete compound, whether attributive like 'rational animal' or additive like 'Zayd's servant'. And it also excludes performatives (insha'at), for these matters do not bear truth and falsehood in themselves. But they may bear it due to an external matter, such as 'Give me water', for it does not bear from the perspective of the concept of request truth or falsehood, but it entails according to custom a declarative relation that bears truth and falsehood, which is 'that he is thirsty'. And likewise the attributive relation, such as 'Zayd the scholar', for it in itself does not admit truth and falsehood, but in it there is an indication to a declarative relation that accepts them, because the immediate understanding is that a thing is not described except by what is established for it. And likewise it is said concerning the additive, since a thing is not added except to what is existing for it. By this consideration the performative and incomplete relation bears truth and falsehood, and that is outside their concepts, and for that reason he added in the definition his saying: 'by itself'.
Source pages p. 573

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on propositions (qadaya) and their rulings. It comments on the definition of a proposition as 'that which bears truth and falsehood' (قوله: احتمال الصدق). The commentator explains that this phrase excludes two types of expressions. First, the incomplete compound (al-murakkab al-naqis), which can be either attributive (taqyidi) like 'rational animal' where the second part qualifies the first, or additive (idafi) like 'Zayd's servant' where the second is possessed by the first. These are not full propositions because they do not form a complete judgment. Second, it excludes performatives (insha'at), such as commands, questions, and exclamations, which by themselves do not have truth-value. For example, the request 'Give me water' is not true or false as a request, but it implies a declarative statement 'he is thirsty' which can be true or false. Similarly, an attributive compound like 'Zayd the scholar' implies a declarative relation that Zayd is characterized by scholarship, because one only describes something with what is actually true of it. The same reasoning applies to additive compounds: saying 'Zayd's servant' implies that Zayd actually possesses a servant. The conclusion is that these relations, whether performative or incomplete, can bear truth and falsehood indirectly, but that is outside their essential concepts. Hence the definition adds 'by itself' (lidhatihi) to indicate that only expressions that are truth-apt in their own right qualify as propositions.

Key Terms
قضية
مركب ناقص
إنشاء
نسبة خبرية
لذاته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the author add 'by itself' (لِذَاتِهِ) to the definition?
A) To exclude incomplete compounds and performatives.
B) To include all speech.
C) To show propositions are self-evident.
D) None of the above.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'by itself' is crucial: a proposition must be truth-apt intrinsically, not through external implication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Propositions
beginner
5 min
Exclusions from the Proposition: Incomplete Compounds and Performatives
Author explains exclusions from proposition definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain why incomplete compounds and performative utterances are not propositions.

Core Idea
Incomplete compounds and performatives are not truth-apt in themselves; they only imply declarative relations.

The commentator explains two categories excluded from the definition: incomplete compounds (like phrases) and performatives (commands, questions, etc.). Understanding these exclusions sharpens our ability to recognize genuine propositions in logical discourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two exclusions
In the passage, the commentator lists two exclusions from the proposition definition: incomplete compounds (al-murakkab al-naqis) and performatives (al-insha'at).
2
Analyze incomplete compounds
Incomplete compounds are phrases that do not form a complete sentence. They are of two types: attributive (taqyidi) like 'rational animal' and additive (idafi) like 'Zayd's servant'. They are not truth-apt because they lack a declarative relation.
The passage gives examples: الحيوان الناطق and غلام زيد.
3
Analyze performatives
Performatives are utterances like commands, questions, and exclamations. They are not truth-apt in themselves. For example, 'Give me water' is a request; it is neither true nor false as a request. However, it implies a declarative statement ('he is thirsty') that can be true or false.
The passage uses اسقني ماء as an example.
4
Understand the implication
The commentator notes that these expressions can bear truth and falsehood indirectly, but that is outside their essential concepts. Hence the definition includes 'by itself' to exclude them.
The addition of لذاته is key.
